Shen Bao Local Supplement

Republic of China Twenty-First Year

January 17, Sunday

(No Additional Charge)

Small Forum

The Resurrection of Japanese Ships and the Unfortunate Exclusion of Chinese Employees

According to this newspaper's report on the 14th, almost all Japanese ships in China have ceased operations and stopped classes due to the boycott since the September 18 Incident. On the Yangtze River route, the original number of Japanese ships, more than 20, has been reduced to three, all of which are air-borne. On the Sino-Japanese route of the Japanese Mail Steamship Company, there are four routes and nine ships in operation. The business is excellent, and the monthly income from passenger tickets alone is 90,000 to 100,000 yuan. In October and November of last year, the monthly income was only 12,000 to 13,000 yuan, a drop of eight-tenths compared to normal. However, recently, my country's anti-Japanese goods movement has been relaxed, and Japanese ships on the Yangtze River have taken the opportunity to reduce fares by 50%. As a result, exports have suddenly surged, and the three special cabins on each trip are all crowded. On the Sino-Japanese route, business income has also suddenly increased, increasing from more than 10,000 yuan last month to about 40,000 yuan.

According to this newspaper's report on the 15th, the Japanese merchant ships in Dalian Bay have already held a meeting and decided that from this month onwards, all Chinese sailors, stokers, etc. used by each ship will be suspended, and the number of unemployed people will be at least 1,000 or more. In addition, there is an even more bizarre piece of news: Zhang Zhengben, the president of my country's Zhengji Shipping Company, suddenly disregarded everything and replaced all the senior crew members of all 23 ships with Japanese, and submitted a request to the Ministry of Transportation, saying that there was a lack of talent among Chinese sailors and that Japanese had to be used. He requested that Japanese be issued shipowner licenses.

After we have read the above two news items, we really want to cry without tears. The lost territory of the Northeast has not yet been recovered, and Jinzhou has recently fallen again. The enemy cavalry is roaring and coming west, and the public spirit that we once agitated and encouraged has returned to a state of sleep. The eighth boycott of Japanese goods is about to end. On the contrary, the Japanese are completely dismissing the Chinese crew members on my country's ships. Who is boycotting whom? Who is the ultimate victor? The Japanese ridiculed our anti-Japanese goods movement as a "childhood disease" and said, "After one boycott, the sales of Japanese goods will inevitably surge." We have really been seen through. O nation that does not strive, what will you use to survive when the last weapon you have in your hand is taken away by the enemy?

As for the manager of Zhengji Shipping Company willingly recognizing the thief as his father, his heart is completely dead, so what more can be said? Even if he were to be hacked to pieces, it would not be enough to cover up his guilt.

Compatriots, for the sake of self-salvation and national salvation, can we bear to give up the last remaining weapon of self-defense in our hands?

Popular Literature

Gambling with Destiny

— Zhou Wu'ai

A bright red large X is squarely pasted on the greasy lamppost. Annoying, ear-splitting gongs and suonas play unnatural tunes from the hands or mouths of several children, reflecting in the doorway that the value of a young woman's life is being gambled away in a game of fate.

The master of ceremonies, wearing a jade-green jacket over a torn cotton robe, chants practiced eulogies that have nothing to do with him from his yellow face, tightly wrapped around bones, and between his teeth stained with grime. Relatives and friends filled the room, and idle onlookers from the neighborhood crowded the courtyard, all quietly holding their breath. Only the master of ceremonies constantly spews out his authority, directing a busy group of men and women and the newlywed bride, adorned with powder and pearls. The bride, under a pair of brightly lit, flickering red candles,

is a nineteen-year-old miss. Her petite figure, adorned with such gorgeous attire, walks gracefully and stands elegantly, further enhancing her inherent beauty with artificial adornment. The silent ones all stirred. The eyes of parents and sisters seemed somewhat reddened. Idle onlookers discussed irrelevant criticisms.

Twisting her slender waist, following the master of ceremonies' direction, she bows and bids farewell incessantly. The emotions of parting make those involved feel lonely. Sadness covers the smiling face that dominates everything, leading her mother to gamble on hope, unable to hold back tears of mixed emotions. A lonely atmosphere occupies several moved hearts amidst the lively scene.

In turn, she approached me. Her lowered face occasionally lifted. Before I could discern the external expression of her inner self, she lowered it again with the repeated words "bow." As I returned the bow, my heart and mind were surging with chaotic memories and fantasies.

She entered the flower sedan chair, its curtain already lifted – a flower sedan chair decorated so that she could not breathe fresh air or see a ray of light. As the curtain was drawn, eight coarse and repulsive porters hoisted her up on their shoulders. Amid shouts and the blare of music, she hid in the darkness, waiting quietly for the gamble of fate to bet on the value of her life!

Smiling in dreams of love, she never walked through a rosy garden, only entrusting her color-blind ideals to the flower sedan chair, waiting for the mystical world to be revealed when the sedan curtain is raised again.

Popular Science

Resurrecting from Ashes

— Tao Xiaotao

"Resurrecting from Ashes" is a trick of nurturing air. It can make an extinguished fire reignite. Since we want to experiment with this trick of nurturing air, we should also know a little about the history of nurturing air.

Tradition has it that nurturing air was discovered by the Englishman Joseph Priestley. In 1774, he obtained this gas by heating red mercuric oxide (i.e., elixir). However, before Priestley, a Swedish chemist named Scheele was actually the first to discover nurturing air.

Scheele used manganese dioxide to invent nurturing air. We can do it once, too. Take a test tube, wipe it dry with a cloth on all sides to prevent it from bursting when heated. Put a spoonful each of manganese dioxide and potassium chlorate into the test tube. Seal the mouth of the tube with a cork. Drill a hole in the middle of the cork, the size of a glass tube, and insert a bent glass tube. Next, take a washbasin (or glass tank) and fill it with a little more than half a basin of water.

Then take a glass, fill it with water, and place it upside down in the water in the washbasin. Next, put the end of the bent glass tube outside the test tube into the bottom of the glass. Then light an alcohol lamp and burn the manganese dioxide in the test tube. The potassium chlorate will react chemically and emit a gas. You will see bubbles emerging in the glass. These bubbles are oxygen bubbles, running one by one into the glass. The water in the glass is gradually pushed down by the nurturing air.

When all the water in the cup is pushed out, use a wire to tie a match, light the match, blow it out, and quickly put the red-hot match head into the cup. You will see the match burn again, even redder than before it was lit, burning until the match is gone.

This experiment proves that nurturing air has the property of helping combustion. You must do this experiment quickly to get good results. This experiment can be done successfully for only two or three dimes.

This nurturing air is the same as the nurturing air in the air. Air contains two-tenths nurturing air. Fire can burn in the air because of nurturing air.

Street Sociology

Various Ways of Making a Living (4) Apricots

Do readers have some spare time? If you have some spare time, you might as well act as a temporary "road inspector" and inspect for a week. You can discover the livelihood of many poor and good people.

As the saying goes, "If a person has no means of livelihood, they will eat up a peck of gold." Moreover, those poor and good common people not only have no peck of gold to sit and eat, but also have no copper tendons and iron bones to work as coolies. They are also unwilling to do evil. In the sinful Shanghai, it is difficult for them not to cheat, steal, plunder, or rob. They rely on their ten fingers to feed their mouths. These good people are also worth talking about.

One day, I saw a compatriot with a sallow face on North Sichuan Road Bridge, standing under the high wall of the post office, basking in the sun, holding a fir box filled with bamboo ear picks and head-scratching and head-washing bamboo utensils. He was sharpening a small bamboo stick in his hand. An ear pick is worth two copper coins, and a head-washing bamboo comb is worth four to six copper coins. Curiosity made me start asking him:

"Is your business good?"

He glanced at me strangely and did not answer. However, I, who "break the casserole and ask to the end," still asked the second sentence:

"How much copper money can you sell in a day?"

"If it's good, I can sell a few dimes, if it's not good, only a few copper plates." He said calmly.

"Are a few dimes enough to eat?"

"If it's not enough, what can I do! Those who have copper money use money to make money, those who kidnap use their lives to make money. People in my business eat when they have food, and starve when they don't."

These words were sincere, but I felt that he was teaching me a lesson.

East, South, West, North

Wen Qing in a Pavilion for Five Yuan a Day

My classmate and good friend, Miss Zhou, dropped out of school due to the tragic changes in her family and the oppression of her environment. She left Shanghai and wandered elsewhere to seek a livelihood for almost two years. Now she has returned to Shanghai to find a school to continue her studies. She

found a pavilion in an alley she used to live in, as a temporary place to settle down.

She had just moved her luggage into the building when the landlady urged her to pay five yuan in rent. She tidied up her luggage and turned on the electric lights in the house. She was quietly sitting on the edge of the bed, resting, when the landlady came in again.

"Miss, please go out and find a guarantor!" the landlady said.

"Find what guarantor?" She stared at the landlady in surprise and said.

"Now, to live in a house in the Chinese Concession, you need to have a guarantor. If you don't find a guarantor to file a guarantee at the police station today, they will come and check, and you will definitely be punished." The landlady said again.

"I am a student, and I will not live here for long. I will move to the school. I don't know anyone in Shanghai. Where can I find a guarantor! Well, if you need a guarantor, please be my guarantor." She said again.

"Originally, for people doing other businesses, the sub-landlord can go to the police station to file a guarantee. Because you are a student, there are many unruly people among the students, so the police station must have a shop guarantee." The landlady said.

"Students are not floods or wild beasts. It's really annoying. There is no freedom to live in Shanghai!" She said in surprise again.

At this time, it was really difficult for her to find a shop guarantee. If she didn't find a shop guarantee, the police station would punish her again. There was no way but to think about moving back to the hotel. So she negotiated with the landlady to return the rent. But when the landlady heard that she wanted to return the five yuan rent, her face immediately changed and she said:

"There is no rule in Shanghai that rent can be returned after it has been paid." She argued with the landlady for a long time, but there was no result. Miss Zhou was so angry that her face turned red. On one hand, she hated the woman's cunning and deceit, and on the other hand, she hated the ruling authorities for not having a fundamental way to maintain social order, causing some pedestrians and travelers to be in a dilemma.

It was late at night, and she risked spending the night in the pavilion. The next morning, she packed her luggage again, called a rickshaw, and went straight to the hotel she had stayed in before.

Small Consumption Statistics

— Xu Shuilin

X Opium and Gambling

Last year, the French envoy ordered the French Concession to ban opium and gambling. It was reported that about 50,000 people in the French Concession rely on opium and gambling for a living. If it is banned, public security cannot be maintained. By analogy, in the combined concessions of the North and South Municipalities, no less than 200,000 people rely on opium and gambling. These people make profits and share profits every day, with direct and indirect living expenses of about 1.5 yuan.

The daily total is 300,000 yuan.

The monthly total is 9 million yuan.

The annual total is 108 million yuan.

If it is 400,000 people, it should be 216 million yuan. Further extrapolation.

Shanghai Stories

Shanghai Stories (12) Compiled and Translated by Zhou Rong

X The Current Site of the British Consulate

British Consul Balfour was originally in Shanghai County. At this time, he was eager to purchase land within the concession to rebuild the new office. However, according to the laws of the British government at the time, foreign consuls were not allowed to purchase land and build public offices. They could only rent houses in the host country as the consulate. However, British Consul Balfour ignored his own country's laws and boldly sought land within the concession to build a consulate.

On April 28, 1846, Balfour purchased a piece of land from the Li family at the northern end of the British Concession, totaling one hundred acres, for a price of 17,000 yuan. Because he had not obtained the permission of the British government, Balfour advanced 4,000 yuan himself. After May, Balfour was discharged and Alcock (Rutherfkrd Alcock) succeeded as consul. After taking over the matter, after many difficulties, he finally obtained the approval of the British government to acknowledge the purchase price of the consulate. The new site of the British Consulate was finally determined. On July 21, 1849, the British Consul moved from the city to the new site in the concession.

The new consulate built in 1852 was destroyed by fire on December 23, 1870. Many documents were reduced to ashes. The current British Consulate was rebuilt in 1872.

Home
